рд╖рд╖реНрдареЗрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХреЗ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ ред тАЬ рднрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рдзреНрд░реНрдпрд╢реНрд╡рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдореН ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреЛ рджреНрд╡реЗ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпрд╛рд╡рде рджрд╢ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рдореНрдпрддреЗ- рднрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд╛рдзреНрд░реНрдпрд╢реНрд╡ рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

69 (869)
Agni
Sumitra V─Бdhrya┼Ыva
12 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 1тАУ2
This hymn is discussed at length and translated in full by Proferes (2007: 40тАУ44), who calls it тАЬperhaps the clearest example of a tribal fire and the ritual role of the clans in relation to this fire. It illustrates the existence of a central fire tended by multiple clans who affirm through it their mutual solidarity, and who see in it the source of their domination over othersтАЭ (p. 40). This particular clan-fire is that of King Vadhrya┼Ыva (see vss. 1тАУ2, 4, 10тАУ12), a speaking name with a deprecatory sense: тАЬpossessing gelded horses,тАЭ and in fact the fire itself bears the patronymic тАЬson/descendant of Vadhrya┼ЫvaтАЭ (see vss. 5, 9, 12). The current fire is also con trasted with fire or fires kindled previously (vss. 4тАУ5), and toward the end of the hymn this fire present here is depicted as victorious over former fires, presumably belonging to other clans (vss. 10тАУ11). Such victories are just an aspect of the victo ries over other peoples that the clan-fire brings Vadhrya┼Ыva and his allies, the men who kindle and tend this fire (vss. 5тАУ6, 9тАУ12).
One curious detail in the hymn is found in verse 7, where various possessions are ascribed to the fire (here called a craftsman), including тАЬa thousand barren cows.тАЭ The negative connotations of this property are immediately counteracted in the next verse (8ab), in which the fire is credited with having an abundantly fertile cow whose flow of milk is inexhaustible, but the great flock of barren cows is nonethe
less odd. It finds its explanation in a semantic pun: just as the triumphant and suc cessful Vadhrya┼Ыva bears the name тАЬpossessing gelded horsesтАЭ so does his equally triumphant and successful fire тАЬpossess barren cows.тАЭ
Stylistically there is much chaining of phraseology and repetition of syntactic patterns.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Agni’s regards be benevolent to Vadhrya┼Ыva; may his guidance be auspicious, his approaches(to the sacrifice) favourable; when the Sumitra people first kindled Agni, then fed with butter and brilliantly blazinghe is glorified.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Auspicious are the manifestations of the fire of Vadhrya┼Ыva; his guidance is valuable; reverent approaches (to him) bring joy.
When the clans that are good allies kindle him at the beginning,
bepoured with ghee he awakens, flashing again and again.

Griffith

Auspicious is the aspect of Vadhryasva’s fire good is its guidance, pleasant are its visitings.
When first the people Of Sumitra kindle it, with butter poured thercon it crackles and shines bright.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay gh─л be the augmenter of the Agni of Vadhrya┼Ыva; may gh─л be his food; may gh─л be hisnutriment; sacrified to with gh─л he expands exceedingly; he shines like the sun, when the clarified butter ispoured out for him.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The strengthener of the fire of Vadhrya┼Ыva is ghee; ghee is his food, ghee his fattener.
Bepoured with ghee, he spreads out widely. He shines like the sunтАФhis potion melted butter.

Griffith

Butter is that which makes Vadhryaiva’s fire growstrong: the butter is its food, the butter makes it fat.
It spreads abroad when butter hath been offered it, and balmed with streams of butter shines forth like the Sun.

Geldner

Schmalz ist St├дrkung f├╝r Vadhryasva┬┤s Feuer, Schmalz seine Speise. Schmalz seine M├дstung. Mit Schmalz begossen dehnt er sich weithin aus; wie die Sonne leuchtet er, dessen Tr├дnklein Schmalz ist.

Grassmann

Fett ist des Agni V─Бdhria├зva Labetrunk, und Fett ihm Speise, fette Butter seine Mast; Mit Fett begossen dehnt er in die Weite sich, mit Schmalz getr├дnkt erstrahlet er der Sonne gleich.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay that your army of flame, Agni, which Manu, which Sumitra has kindled, be the newest; do youshine wealthily; do you graciously accept our praises; do you destroy the might (of our foes), do you grant usabundance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Which face of yours Manu kindled, which (did) the good ally, o Agni, that is this one here anew.
Blaze richly; take pleasure in the songs. Break out the prize; confer
fame here.

Griffith

Still newest is this face of thine, O Agni, which Manu and Sumitra have enkindled.
So richly shine, accept our songs with favour, so give us strengthening food, so send us glory.

Geldner

Dein Antlitz, das Manu, das Sumitra entflammt hat, o Agni, dies ist auch das allerneueste. Flamme prangend, hab an der Lobrede Gefallen, schlag Lohn heraus, bringe Ruhm ein!

Grassmann

Die Glanzgestalt, die Manu, die Sumitra dir hat entflammt, die strahlt, o Agni, neu hier; So leuchte hell, nimm freundlich an die Lieder, erschliesse Gut, und schenk uns reiche Sch├дtze.

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Agni, whom Vadhrya┼Ыva propitiating you formerly kindled, accept this; be the proector of oursacrifices, be the protector of our bodies; preserve this wealth which has been given to us by you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You whom Vadhrya┼Ыva, when reverently invoked, kindled formerly, o Agni, do you take pleasure in this (new face) here.
Become the protector of our people and the protector of our own
bodies. Guard the giftтАФwhatever you have for us here.

Griffith

Accept this offering, Agni, whom aforetime Vadhryasva, hath entreated and enkindled.
Guard well our homes and ople, guard our bodies, protect thy girt to us which thou hast granted.

Geldner

English translation:

тАЬKinsman of Vadhrya┼Ыva, be the possessor of food and our protector; let no one assail you, (for youare) the overcomer of men; like a resolute warrior (you are) the overthrower (of enemies); I, Sumitra, celebratethe names of the kinsmen of Vadhya┼Ыva.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Become possessed of brilliance, o son of Vadhrya┼Ыva, and our herdsman. Let the hostile intent of the peoples not overtake you.
A rouser like a bold champion, a good allyтАФI shall now proclaim the name of Vadhrya┼ЫvaтАЩs son.

Griffith

Be splendid, guard us Kinsman of Vadhryasva: let not the enmity of men o’ercome thee,
Like the bold hero Cyavana, I Sumitra tell forth the title of Vadhryaiva’s Kinsman.

English translation:

тАЬYou have gained mountain-treasures beneficial to men, (you have defeated the hostilities) of strongmen, D─Бsas and Vс╣Ыtras, like a resolute warrior, do you, Agni, the overthrower (of enemies), overcome thosewho are desirous of battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The goods of the plains and the mountains, the D─Бsa and the ─Аrya obstaclesтАФyou have conquered them entirely.
A rouser of the peoples like a bold championтАФyou, o Agni, should
dominate those who seek battle.

Griffith

All treasures hast thou won, of plains and mountains, and quelled the Dasas’ and Aryas’ hatred.
Like the bold hero Cyavana, O Agni, mayst thou subdue the men who long for battle.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis Agni to whom a long series (of sacrifices has been addressed), who is bright with many rays,covering thousands (in the form of gh─л), the leader of hundreds (of burnt offerings), the mighty one, brilliantamong the brilliant, (is) being glorified by the priests; shine (Agni) upon the devout Sumitras.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

To whom a longserieс╣г..: liс╣н, long-threaded, large-oxed, thousand- heifered, hundred-guider

Jamison Brereton

This fire here has a long thread and lofty oxen; the craftsman has a thousand barren cows and a hundred counsels.
Brilliant among the brilliant (gods), being groomed by men, you will shine among the good allies who seek the gods.1494 X.70

Griffith

Deft Agni hath a lengthened thread, tall oxen, a thousand heifers, numberless devices.
Decked by the men, splendid among the splendid, shine brightly forth amid devout Sumitras.

Geldner

Dieser Agni spinnt einen langen Faden, f├дhrt mit gro├Яen Stieren; er hat tausend Geltk├╝he, hundert Schliche, der Meister. Unter den Gl├дnzenden gl├дnzend, von den Herren herausgeputzt, sollst du bei den gottergebenen Sumitra┬┤s leuchten.

Grassmann

Der langen Faden webt, der hohe Stiere, und tausend K├╝he hat und hundert Bahnen, Du starker Agni strahlest hell bei hellen, erzeugt von M├дnnern bei den frommen Freunden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn you, J─Бtavedas, is the cow easy to be milked, yielding ambrosia as it were inexhaustibly in battle,you are kindled, Agni, by the devout Sumitras who are entitled to the sacrificial donation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yieldingambrosia…battle: asa┼Ыcateva saman─Б = united with the sun which has no association, i.e., is not joined toanything because it has no settled home

Jamison Brereton

O J─Бtavedas, in you is the milk-cow, yielding good milk, milking out nectar always in the same way, like the two [=Heaven and Earth] that never dry up.
You, Agni, are kindled by men who receive the priestly gifts, by the good allies who seek the gods.

Griffith

Thine is the teeming cow, O Jatavedas, who pours at once her ceaseless flow, Sabardhuk,
Thou. art lit up by men enriched with guerdon, O Agni, by the pious-souled Sumitras.

Geldner

Dein ist die gutmelke Kuh, o Jatavedas, die wie die unversieglichen Rodasi immer gleichm├д├Яig frische Milch gibt. Du wirst von den Opferlohn spendenden Herren, von den gottergebenen Sumitra┬┤s angez├╝ndet, o Agni.

Grassmann

O Wesenkenner, dir geh├╢rt die Milchkuh, die wie in stetem Gusse Nektar ausstr├╢mt; Du Agni wirst von gabenreichen M├дnnern entflammt und von den eifrigen Sumitra’s.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe immortal gods have proclaimed your greatness. J─Бtavedas, Vadhrya┼Ыva (Agni); when humanbeings, came to inquire (who would slay the asuras), then you with (the gods), the leaders of all, fostered by youdid overcome (those who impeded the ceremony).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Even the immortal gods proclaimed your greatness, o J─Бtavedas, son of Vadhrya┼Ыva.
When the clans of the sons of Manu came to negotiate, you conquered by means of the men whose strength is you.

Griffith

Even Immortal Gods, O Jatavedas, Vadhryasva’s Kinsman, have declared thy grandeur.
When human tribes drew near with supplication thou conqueredst with men whom thou hadst strengthened.

Geldner

Selbst die unsterblichen G├╢tter verk├╝nden deine Gr├╢├Яe, o Jatavedas, Kind des Vadhryasva. Als die menschlichen Clane kamen, um bei dir sich Rat zu holen, da siegtest du mit den durch dich stark gewordenen Herren.

Grassmann

Die ew’gen G├╢tter selbst, o Wesenkenner, o V─Бdhria├зva, r├╝hmten deine Gr├╢sse; Als bittend dir der Menschen St├дmme nahten, da siegtest du durch M├дnner, die du st├дrktest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVadhrya┼Ыva, honouring you, Agni, plural ced you upon the altar as a father (plural ces) his son (upon hislap); plural ased with his fuel, youngest (of the gods), you did slay the ancient obstructers of the rite.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like a father his son, Vadhrya┼Ыva bore you on his lap as he served you, o Agni.
And taking pleasure in his kindling, o youngest one, you vanquished the former (fires), even though they were greatly arrogant.

Griffith

Thou, Youngest God, having enjoyed his fuel, didst vanquish those of old though they were mighty.

English translation:

тАЬAgni by means of the priests of Vadhrya┼Ыva pouring out libations always conquers his foes; you(Agni) shining with varied splendour, have consumed the battle; (your praiser) self-fostered has destroyed hispowerful (assailant).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Over and over the fire of Vadhrya┼Ыva has conquered rivals by means of the men that provide the pressed soma.
You burned even the (whole) crowd, o bright-beamed one; as
strengthener you cut down even the greatly arrogant one.

Griffith

Vadhryasva’s Agni evermore hath vanquished his foes with heroes who had pressed the Soma.
Lord of bright rays, thou burntest up the battle, subduing, as our help, e’en mighty foemen.

Geldner

Immer wieder hat des Vadhryasva Agni die Feinde besiegt im Bunde mit den somapressenden Herren. Du branntest die Schlachtreihe nieder, du Prachtglanz; du hast den, der sich st├дrker f├╝hlte als selbst der Starke, herabgehauen.

Besiegt hat Agni stets des Vadhria├зva Bek├дmpfer durch der Somapresser Freunde, Den Tross auch hast verbrannt du strahlenreicher, zerschmettert auch den Trotzenden als Helfer.

English translation:

тАЬFrom a long period has this Agni the slayer of foes been kindled (by the oblation) of Vadhrya┼Ыva; (heis) to be addressed with reverence; do you, (Agni, kindled in the) family of Vadhrya┼Ыva, overcome our enemies,both those who have no kinsmen and those who have many kinsmen.тАЭ

Here is the fire of Vadhrya┼Ыva, the smasher of Vr╠еtra, kindled from of old, to be addressed with reverence.

This Agni of Vadhryasva, Vrtra-slayer, lit from of old, must be invoked with homage.
As such assail our enemies, Vadhryasva, whether the foes be strangers or be kinsmen.
